    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
  
    function getParent() {
      return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
  
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }
  
      var style = doc.createElement('style');
      style.id = id;
      style.innerHTML = def;
      parent.appendChild(style);
    }

      if (!parent) {
        return;
      }

        return;
      }
  
      parent.removeChild(style);
    }

<div class="cmp-title" id="title-a2e1400738" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-a2e1400738&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;(Micro)Segmentation from a Practical Perspective | Akamai&#34;}}">
    
      <h1 class="cmp-title__text">(Micro)Segmentation from a Practical Perspective</h1>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="section section__vertical-center aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

  
  
  
      

      

  <div class="cmp-section   " data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;section-59a9a9c029&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/section&#34;}}">
    
    
  
    
      <div class="cmp-section__row 1 cmp-section__2-columns">
        <div class="cmp-section__row-wrapper cmp-section__two-column--separate ">
          <div class="columns column-1  fifty-fifty">
            




    
    
    <div class="blogauthor">

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-02418ffc30" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-02418ffc30&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T02:38:00Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Introduction&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Introduction</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5d6f57fd2d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-12T17:13:30Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Network segmentation is difficult to implement. No, scratch that. &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/glossary/what-is-microsegmentation.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Network segmentation&lt;/a> is easy to implement; segmenting the network in a way that doesn’t impact the end user or network operability while making it secure is nigh impossible.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We (the Akamai Security Intelligence Group researchers) often mention network segmentation as a mitigation strategy for &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/linux-lateral-movement-more-than-ssh.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>lateral movement&lt;/a> and the various other threats we report on — whether it’s in our &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.akamai.com/search?q=%22Akamai%E2%80%99s%20Perspective%20on%22%2B%22Patch%20Tuesday%22&amp;amp;size=n_10_n\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Patch Tuesday advisories&lt;/a>, our malware reports, vulnerability advisories, or other research pieces. &lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In this post, we’ll provide practical, concrete segmentation strategies and realistic best practices for defenders. Our aim is to only discuss segmentation strategies that are actionable and would not affect network operability or end-user experience very much while still having a significant security benefit.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Although proper segmentation is challenging, there are some quick wins when it comes to protecting your network. To highlight this, we’ve included several &lt;a href=\&#34;#cyberattack-kill-chain\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>segmentation strategies&lt;/a> that deal with different stages of a network breach. &lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;i>Please note that real-world networks differ from one another; although we aim to provide general recommendations, the strategies may require adjustments to be applicable for you&lt;/i>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Network segmentation is difficult to implement. No, scratch that. <a href="/glossary/what-is-microsegmentation" target="_self">Network segmentation</a> is easy to implement; segmenting the network in a way that doesn’t impact the end user or network operability while making it secure is nigh impossible.</p>
<p>We (the Akamai Security Intelligence Group researchers) often mention network segmentation as a mitigation strategy for <a href="/blog/security-research/linux-lateral-movement-more-than-ssh" target="_self">lateral movement</a> and the various other threats we report on — whether it’s in our <a href="https://www.akamai.com/search?q=%22Akamai%E2%80%99s%20Perspective%20on%22%2B%22Patch%20Tuesday%22&amp;size=n_10_n" target="_self">Patch Tuesday advisories</a>, our malware reports, vulnerability advisories, or other research pieces. </p>
<p>In this post, we’ll provide practical, concrete segmentation strategies and realistic best practices for defenders. Our aim is to only discuss segmentation strategies that are actionable and would not affect network operability or end-user experience very much while still having a significant security benefit.</p>
<p>Although proper segmentation is challenging, there are some quick wins when it comes to protecting your network. To highlight this, we’ve included several <a href="#cyberattack-kill-chain" target="_self">segmentation strategies</a> that deal with different stages of a network breach. </p>
<p><i>Please note that real-world networks differ from one another; although we aim to provide general recommendations, the strategies may require adjustments to be applicable for you</i>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="button button__large-button button__cta-blue button__white-text button__border-cta-blue button__dark-hover button__left button__fullWidth-mobile aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    <span class="cmp-button__text">Linux user? Fight lateral movement</span>
    
</a>

  

</div>

<div class="title title__paddingTop-40 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="network-segmentation" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;network-segmentation&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:15:53Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;What is network segmentation?&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">What is network segmentation?<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5c76ee9024&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T02:59:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Before we can jump into best practices and strategies, we first need to define our playground. Network segmentation involves “breaking” the network into parts (segments) and defining who can access what, and in what way (for example, web servers may only be accessed via HTTP/S).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Traditionally, this has been achieved using VLANs and physical firewalls, but lately we see more and more software-based approaches to firewalls and segmentation (&lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/products/akamai-guardicore-segmentation.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Akamai Guardicore Segmentation&lt;/a>, for example). We won’t recommend one way or the other — there are pros and cons to both approaches. Our recommended policies and strategies are vendor-agnostic and can apply everywhere.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When you move on from controlling traffic using VLANs, access control lists (ACLs), and IP ranges to using custom labels that are vendor-agnostic, you enter the realm of microsegmentation. &lt;b>All our strategies in this blog post will assume that we’re using microsegmentation&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>It should be possible to adapt the strategies and guidelines to not require segmentation, but the process to define all the VLANs, ACLs, and IP lists, and then maintain them is probably impractical, or will come with the immediate burnout of all network admins and engineers. (Try to define the IP range/group of all finance servers. It might be doable, but can you maintain that list accurately for long? That’s also only one server group; in an enterprise network, you’ll have many more — end users, domain controllers, domain admins, printers, etc.)&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Before we can jump into best practices and strategies, we first need to define our playground. Network segmentation involves “breaking” the network into parts (segments) and defining who can access what, and in what way (for example, web servers may only be accessed via HTTP/S). </p>
<p>Traditionally, this has been achieved using VLANs and physical firewalls, but lately we see more and more software-based approaches to firewalls and segmentation (<a href="/products/akamai-guardicore-segmentation" target="_self">Akamai Guardicore Segmentation</a>, for example). We won’t recommend one way or the other — there are pros and cons to both approaches. Our recommended policies and strategies are vendor-agnostic and can apply everywhere.</p>
<p>When you move on from controlling traffic using VLANs, access control lists (ACLs), and IP ranges to using custom labels that are vendor-agnostic, you enter the realm of microsegmentation. <b>All our strategies in this blog post will assume that we’re using microsegmentation</b>.</p>
<p>It should be possible to adapt the strategies and guidelines to not require segmentation, but the process to define all the VLANs, ACLs, and IP lists, and then maintain them is probably impractical, or will come with the immediate burnout of all network admins and engineers. (Try to define the IP range/group of all finance servers. It might be doable, but can you maintain that list accurately for long? That’s also only one server group; in an enterprise network, you’ll have many more — end users, domain controllers, domain admins, printers, etc.)</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="guidelines" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;guidelines&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:18:03Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Network segmentation guidelines&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Network segmentation guidelines<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ecb7b11b77&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:00:36Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Before we can discuss how to segment, we need to discuss a major prerequisite for it: visibility. Microsegmentation does not live in a vacuum. You can’t protect what you can’t see. &lt;b>Good segmentation is only effective alongside network visibility that organizes and summarizes the traffic&lt;/b>. There is usually too much traffic to realistically parse it all raw with the naked eye.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Before we can discuss how to segment, we need to discuss a major prerequisite for it: visibility. Microsegmentation does not live in a vacuum. You can’t protect what you can’t see. <b>Good segmentation is only effective alongside network visibility that organizes and summarizes the traffic</b>. There is usually too much traffic to realistically parse it all raw with the naked eye.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="A side-by-side comparison of network traffic visualization. Left: a visual map of traffic and connections. Right: a screenshot from Wireshark, a network sniffing tool, that shows raw packet summary." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-999a5c20a1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-12T17:14:35Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;A side-by-side comparison of network traffic visualization. Left: a visual map of traffic and connections. Right: a screenshot from Wireshark, a network sniffing tool, that shows raw packet summary.&#34;,&#34;xdm:linkURL&#34;:&#34;/site/en/images/blog/2023/network-visibility.png&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;ad8f9cbd-bde7-4a9e-9796-da5dd33fcb97&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:11:57Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/network-visibility.png&#34;}}}">
    
      <a class="cmp-image__link" href="/site/en/images/blog/2023/network-visibility.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer" data-cmp-hook-image="link">
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/network-visibility.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="A side-by-side comparison of network traffic visualization. Left: a visual map of traffic and connections. Right: a screenshot from Wireshark, a network sniffing tool, that shows raw packet summary."/>
        
        
      </a>
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 1: Network visibility via a visibility tool vs. raw data via network sniffing</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-a23d08ccca&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:37:24Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>You can see in Figure 1 that there’s a lot of traffic going on inside that network (and there’s also a dummy network in the figure for illustration purposes). Creating policies that apply to each and every traffic strand that moves through the network is realistically impossible.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Instead, we can focus on small scale segmentation mini-projects that improve the security bit by bit (remember, it’s &lt;i>microsegmentation&lt;/i>, not &lt;i>macrosegmentation&lt;/i>). Although having an overarching goal is good, it’s probably better to focus on increasing security gradually, based on your network’s threat model.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>What is &lt;a href=\&#34;https://owasp.org/www-community/Threat_Modeling\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>threat modeling&lt;/a>? It’s a way of defining the type of threats and &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/glossary/what-is-a-cyber-attack.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>cyberattacks&lt;/a>&amp;nbsp;you’re expecting to deal with, and defining priorities accordingly. For example, small and medium-sized businesses are unlikely to encounter state-sponsored threat actors, but &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.ibtimes.co.uk/lazarus-north-korean-hackers-suspected-have-stolen-millions-taiwan-bank-cyberheist-1643408\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>banks on the other hand, might&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If you store a lot of sensitive information, your biggest threat might be &lt;a href=\&#34;#exfiltration\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>data exfiltration&lt;/a>. Smaller businesses may want to focus more on their &lt;a href=\&#34;#initial-access\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>perimeter&lt;/a>, since they may not have a lot of machines inside the network to properly break into segments. If you’re scared of attackers running rampant in your network, consider starting with &lt;a href=\&#34;#lateral-movement\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>lateral movement segmentation&lt;/a>. Do you have a business critical application that must not fall into the wrong hands? You can start by &lt;a href=\&#34;#general-segmention\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>ringfencing&lt;/a> it.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>You can see in Figure 1 that there’s a lot of traffic going on inside that network (and there’s also a dummy network in the figure for illustration purposes). Creating policies that apply to each and every traffic strand that moves through the network is realistically impossible. </p>
<p>Instead, we can focus on small scale segmentation mini-projects that improve the security bit by bit (remember, it’s <i>microsegmentation</i>, not <i>macrosegmentation</i>). Although having an overarching goal is good, it’s probably better to focus on increasing security gradually, based on your network’s threat model.</p>
<p>What is <a href="https://owasp.org/www-community/Threat_Modeling" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">threat modeling</a>? It’s a way of defining the type of threats and <a href="/glossary/what-is-a-cyber-attack" target="_self">cyberattacks</a> you’re expecting to deal with, and defining priorities accordingly. For example, small and medium-sized businesses are unlikely to encounter state-sponsored threat actors, but <a href="https://www.ibtimes.co.uk/lazarus-north-korean-hackers-suspected-have-stolen-millions-taiwan-bank-cyberheist-1643408" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">banks on the other hand, might</a>.</p>
<p>If you store a lot of sensitive information, your biggest threat might be <a href="#exfiltration" target="_self">data exfiltration</a>. Smaller businesses may want to focus more on their <a href="#initial-access" target="_self">perimeter</a>, since they may not have a lot of machines inside the network to properly break into segments. If you’re scared of attackers running rampant in your network, consider starting with <a href="#lateral-movement" target="_self">lateral movement segmentation</a>. Do you have a business critical application that must not fall into the wrong hands? You can start by <a href="#general-segmention" target="_self">ringfencing</a> it.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="segmentation-policy" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;segmentation-policy&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:24:48Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;How to design a segmentation policy&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">How to design a segmentation policy<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e522044b83&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:19:47Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Before jumping into actual segmentation strategies, we’d like to discuss some guidelines, or principles, that we believe are crucial for good segmentation.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Before jumping into actual segmentation strategies, we’d like to discuss some guidelines, or principles, that we believe are crucial for good segmentation.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-19f7828dc8" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-19f7828dc8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:20:40Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;The more accessible something is, the less output it should be allowed to send&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">The more accessible something is, the less output it should be allowed to send<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-f0282397a4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:21:29Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Generally speaking, servers that have a lot of incoming traffic are more on the handling side of requests, like web or file servers (even domain controllers fall under this category). As such, there shouldn’t be that much outgoing traffic from them, or at least it should be strictly defined.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition, having minimal restrictions on both output and input runs the risk of the server being used as a pivot by attackers since the servers are more accessible for attackers and can be used to access a wider part of the network.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Generally speaking, servers that have a lot of incoming traffic are more on the handling side of requests, like web or file servers (even domain controllers fall under this category). As such, there shouldn’t be that much outgoing traffic from them, or at least it should be strictly defined. </p>
<p>In addition, having minimal restrictions on both output and input runs the risk of the server being used as a pivot by attackers since the servers are more accessible for attackers and can be used to access a wider part of the network.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-7f3b4211a9" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-7f3b4211a9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:22:12Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Use other defense mechanisms where your policy has to be loose&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Use other defense mechanisms where your policy has to be loose<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9439b5d25d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:40:12Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>There are some machines for which policies have to be loose, as there’s too much variability in the traffic coming out of the machine; therefore, many exceptions have to be made.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Take, for example, jump box servers — different users use them to connect to different servers with different protocols. You won’t be able to cover all use cases without being too permissive (which defeats the whole purpose of segmentation).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In such cases, we believe that it’s best to employ other &lt;a href=\&#34;#defense\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>defense mechanisms&lt;/a> instead, and make them stricter (like using stronger user access control for the jump box example, or lower alert thresholds for monitoring services).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>There are some machines for which policies have to be loose, as there’s too much variability in the traffic coming out of the machine; therefore, many exceptions have to be made. </p>
<p>Take, for example, jump box servers — different users use them to connect to different servers with different protocols. You won’t be able to cover all use cases without being too permissive (which defeats the whole purpose of segmentation). </p>
<p>In such cases, we believe that it’s best to employ other <a href="#defense" target="_self">defense mechanisms</a> instead, and make them stricter (like using stronger user access control for the jump box example, or lower alert thresholds for monitoring services).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="title-b34f286634" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;title-b34f286634&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:24:33Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Segmentation doesn’t exist in a vacuum&lt;br>\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Segmentation doesn’t exist in a vacuum<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-0330bea127&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:25:36Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Just because some traffic strand already exists when you start segmenting doesn’t mean you should allow it. Sometimes you’ll have to modify existing configurations of applications or servers when you decide the traffic they produce is unnecessary. Sometimes, you’ll also have to consult existing configurations to understand why certain traffic exists in the first place.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Just because some traffic strand already exists when you start segmenting doesn’t mean you should allow it. Sometimes you’ll have to modify existing configurations of applications or servers when you decide the traffic they produce is unnecessary. Sometimes, you’ll also have to consult existing configurations to understand why certain traffic exists in the first place.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="cyberattack-kill-chain" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;cyberattack-kill-chain&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:26:06Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Breaking the cyberattack kill chain&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Breaking the cyberattack kill chain<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9d2cb932c3&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T03:26:55Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Roughly speaking, we can break down the cyberattack kill chain into three parts:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Network initial access&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Lateral movement phase&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Machine postbreach operations&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&lt;p>The postbreach operations are the operations that attackers are usually performing on each machine in the network that they manage to breach, and those operations change according to the attack campaign. For example, &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/mexals-cryptojacking-malware-resurgence.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>cryptojacking campaigns&lt;/a> will install and run cryptominers, while ransomware campaigns will exfiltrate sensitive data and then encrypt it.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We’ll discuss how segmentation can help in protecting against some parts of the kill chain&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>(Figure 2).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Roughly speaking, we can break down the cyberattack kill chain into three parts:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Network initial access</p>
</li>
<li><p>Lateral movement phase </p>
</li>
<li><p>Machine postbreach operations </p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The postbreach operations are the operations that attackers are usually performing on each machine in the network that they manage to breach, and those operations change according to the attack campaign. For example, <a href="/blog/security-research/mexals-cryptojacking-malware-resurgence" target="_self">cryptojacking campaigns</a> will install and run cryptominers, while ransomware campaigns will exfiltrate sensitive data and then encrypt it. </p>
<p>We’ll discuss how segmentation can help in protecting against some parts of the kill chain </p>
<p>(Figure 2).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="The ransomware kill chain. It starts with initial access, is followed by lateral movement, exfiltration and encryption, and ends with a ransom note and potential profit (for the ransomware operators)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-196aaba765&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:43:44Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;The ransomware kill chain. It starts with initial access, is followed by lateral movement, exfiltration and encryption, and ends with a ransom note and potential profit (for the ransomware operators).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;bebbc86a-409f-4c88-82a2-1b1824515343&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:43:36Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/ransomware-killchain.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/ransomware-killchain.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="The ransomware kill chain. It starts with initial access, is followed by lateral movement, exfiltration and encryption, and ends with a ransom note and potential profit (for the ransomware operators)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 2: The ransomware kill chain</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="initial-access" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;initial-access&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:27:36Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Initial access&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Initial access<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-44b454a796&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-12T01:17:00Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>In this case, segmentation is just like traditional firewalling: you block incoming traffic from outside your network that shouldn’t come in. This would usually be from the internet, but it can also be from third-party networks that are connected to your own. &lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>So, blocking exposed Secure Shell (SSH) or remote desktop protocol (RDP) ports (or basically any port in the &lt;a href=\&#34;#lateral-movement\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>lateral movement&lt;/a> section) is advised. In fact, &lt;b>it’s better to use an allowlist rather than denylist&lt;/b> for traffic that originates from outside your network, especially from the internet (consider, for example, how many internet scanners are active at any given moment).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>In this case, segmentation is just like traditional firewalling: you block incoming traffic from outside your network that shouldn’t come in. This would usually be from the internet, but it can also be from third-party networks that are connected to your own. </p>
<p>So, blocking exposed Secure Shell (SSH) or remote desktop protocol (RDP) ports (or basically any port in the <a href="#lateral-movement" target="_self">lateral movement</a> section) is advised. In fact, <b>it’s better to use an allowlist rather than denylist</b> for traffic that originates from outside your network, especially from the internet (consider, for example, how many internet scanners are active at any given moment).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti initial access segmentation. (1) Block incoming traffic from the internet that can be used for remote control or execution, like RDP, SSH, or SMB. (2) Restrict the internet sources that are allowed to enter your network with a maintainable allowlist. (3) Allow internet access only to machines that must be exposed to the internet, like web servers." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-e544845281&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:14:46Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;81aafb3e-405f-4892-b3a6-6eca9baa269a&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:14:28Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-one.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-one.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti initial access segmentation. (1) Block incoming traffic from the internet that can be used for remote control or execution, like RDP, SSH, or SMB. (2) Restrict the internet sources that are allowed to enter your network with a maintainable allowlist. (3) Allow internet access only to machines that must be exposed to the internet, like web servers."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-6f19455743&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T16:44:14Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Of course, as with any other security tool, practice (or policy) segmentation is not a catch-all for threats. In this case, segmentation can’t cover all initial access vectors, and relying only on segmentation leaves your network exposed to risk. Many breaches begin with phishing emails or links or other forms of social engineering.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Some breaches also begin with vulnerabilities in protocols that should be allowed, or with weak credentials to services that are legitimately exposed to the internet, like the VPN server. Because of that, we recommend not relying just on segmentation to prevent initial access, and employ security solutions for host and email protection in addition to segmentation.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Of course, as with any other security tool, practice (or policy) segmentation is not a catch-all for threats. In this case, segmentation can’t cover all initial access vectors, and relying only on segmentation leaves your network exposed to risk. Many breaches begin with phishing emails or links or other forms of social engineering. </p>
<p>Some breaches also begin with vulnerabilities in protocols that should be allowed, or with weak credentials to services that are legitimately exposed to the internet, like the VPN server. Because of that, we recommend not relying just on segmentation to prevent initial access, and employ security solutions for host and email protection in addition to segmentation.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="lateral-movement" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;lateral-movement&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:30:09Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Lateral movement&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Lateral movement<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-a3adddde91&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T16:45:15Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>There are many ways to execute lateral movement; we will not be covering all of them. Specifically, we’ll focus on preventing lateral movement that can happen through legitimate processes that already exist on the machine, using protocols like RDP or SSH, RPC-based services like the service manager or task scheduler, management tools like PowerShell or WMI, or some of the protocols and tools available in Linux that we discussed in a separate &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/blog/security-research/linux-lateral-movement-more-than-ssh.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>post&lt;/a>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We will not be discussing one-day or zero-day vulnerabilities because they can be in any product and with different implementations, so it’s impractical to have a general strategy that applies to them. The only thing we can recommend is segmentation, since something that is inaccessible is a lot harder to exploit.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Before we dive into different considerations for each of the different protocols, there are two principles that apply to all of them.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>There are many ways to execute lateral movement; we will not be covering all of them. Specifically, we’ll focus on preventing lateral movement that can happen through legitimate processes that already exist on the machine, using protocols like RDP or SSH, RPC-based services like the service manager or task scheduler, management tools like PowerShell or WMI, or some of the protocols and tools available in Linux that we discussed in a separate <a href="/blog/security-research/linux-lateral-movement-more-than-ssh" target="_self">post</a>.</p>
<p>We will not be discussing one-day or zero-day vulnerabilities because they can be in any product and with different implementations, so it’s impractical to have a general strategy that applies to them. The only thing we can recommend is segmentation, since something that is inaccessible is a lot harder to exploit.</p>
<p>Before we dive into different considerations for each of the different protocols, there are two principles that apply to all of them.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti lateral movement segmentation. (1) Strict control over traffic between user machines. (2) Strict control over internet access" class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-c21cbae31c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:15:21Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;61e9791d-0c09-4340-99a4-8ab083650029&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:15:08Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-two.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-two.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti lateral movement segmentation. (1) Strict control over traffic between user machines. (2) Strict control over internet access"/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-74ed6e848a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:46:03Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>&lt;b>Users don’t really need to access other users’ machines, especially not over the network&lt;/b>. Unless someone works in IT, there isn’t a lot of justification for them to connect to another user’s machine remotely. As such, it should be pretty feasible to restrict traffic among users’ machines without compromising network operability very much.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition, since the protocols discussed in this section can be used for remote control or execution, they can also serve as initial access vectors. That’s why we reiterate the need to restrict arbitrary internet access over these protocols.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p><b>Users don’t really need to access other users’ machines, especially not over the network</b>. Unless someone works in IT, there isn’t a lot of justification for them to connect to another user’s machine remotely. As such, it should be pretty feasible to restrict traffic among users’ machines without compromising network operability very much.</p>
<p>In addition, since the protocols discussed in this section can be used for remote control or execution, they can also serve as initial access vectors. That’s why we reiterate the need to restrict arbitrary internet access over these protocols.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ce36cc5e6a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T16:46:59Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;table>\r\n&lt;tbody>&lt;tr>&lt;th>&lt;p>Tool/Protocol&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;th>&lt;p>Port(s)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>RDP&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>3389&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>VNC&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>5900+&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>X Window System&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>6000+&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>TeamViewer&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>5938, 80, 443&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>AnyDesk&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>6568, 80, 443&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>SSH&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>22&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>MS-RPC&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>135, 49152+&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>SMB&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>445, 139&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>WinRM&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>5985, 5986&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>SNMP&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>161&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>rexec&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>512&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>rlogin&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>513&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>rsh&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>514&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;/tbody>&lt;/table>\r\n&#34;}}">

<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="rdp" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;rdp&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:35:24Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;RDP, VNC, TeamViewer, and other remote desktop protocols&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">RDP, VNC, TeamViewer, and other remote desktop protocols</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-c612f6a142&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T16:48:19Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Since these services are interactive and graphical, their automated usage is pretty limited. Therefore, you can expect to not see those protocols used among servers very often (the keyword being “expect” — if you do see it, it’s time to investigate why).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The same reasoning applies among users’ machines — users shouldn’t need to connect to one another. Exceptions to these assumptions might be jump boxes and terminal servers that allow users to hop environments or access servers, IT personnel connections to user machines, or application owners connecting to the application server.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Handling such exceptions should be done by creating suitable policies using segmentation, but those efforts should be supplemented with proper identity access management (IAM) solutions as well.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Since these services are interactive and graphical, their automated usage is pretty limited. Therefore, you can expect to not see those protocols used among servers very often (the keyword being “expect” — if you do see it, it’s time to investigate why). </p>
<p>The same reasoning applies among users’ machines — users shouldn’t need to connect to one another. Exceptions to these assumptions might be jump boxes and terminal servers that allow users to hop environments or access servers, IT personnel connections to user machines, or application owners connecting to the application server. </p>
<p>Handling such exceptions should be done by creating suitable policies using segmentation, but those efforts should be supplemented with proper identity access management (IAM) solutions as well.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for remote desktop protocols. (1) Restrict RDPs to and from user machines. (2) Restrict RDPs among servers. (3) Allow IT machines to use RDPs. (4) Use jump box servers for administrative access or remote control. Allow users access to jump box servers." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-fc1477cd4a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:16:04Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;0163841f-8689-45ec-9a35-0db2a79d2551&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:15:54Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-three.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-three.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for remote desktop protocols. (1) Restrict RDPs to and from user machines. (2) Restrict RDPs among servers. (3) Allow IT machines to use RDPs. (4) Use jump box servers for administrative access or remote control. Allow users access to jump box servers."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1a9955adbb&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:47:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Threat actors sometimes install third-party remote desktop servers as a backdoor and as a persistence method. &lt;b>If you detect remote desktop traffic or software that is new to the network, investigate it&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Threat actors sometimes install third-party remote desktop servers as a backdoor and as a persistence method. <b>If you detect remote desktop traffic or software that is new to the network, investigate it</b>.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="ssh" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;ssh&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:35:33Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;SSH&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">SSH</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-3c0192dafc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T16:50:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Although SSH is similar in concept to the RDPs, the story is more complicated. Since SSH is terminal (text)–based, it is a lot easier to use it to interact with software, and there are programs and scripts that use it. In addition to that, SSH is also used to encapsulate less-secure protocols, like SFTP, which is the SSH encapsulation of the file transfer protocol.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>For those reasons, SSH requires a much more granular approach than other RDPs. Without proper visibility into network traffic, it will be very difficult to properly segment SSH without affecting the end users or network operability.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Although SSH is similar in concept to the RDPs, the story is more complicated. Since SSH is terminal (text)–based, it is a lot easier to use it to interact with software, and there are programs and scripts that use it. In addition to that, SSH is also used to encapsulate less-secure protocols, like SFTP, which is the SSH encapsulation of the file transfer protocol.</p>
<p>For those reasons, SSH requires a much more granular approach than other RDPs. Without proper visibility into network traffic, it will be very difficult to properly segment SSH without affecting the end users or network operability.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for SSH. (1) Microsegment SSH based on existing traffic and logical units. (2) Allow IT personnel and application owners to have SSH access to required servers. (3) Restrict arbitrary user SSH access to and from jump box servers." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-d86142f5d1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:16:37Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;114352eb-2cb4-47d3-871d-2e7118d937a5&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:16:27Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-four.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-four.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for SSH. (1) Microsegment SSH based on existing traffic and logical units. (2) Allow IT personnel and application owners to have SSH access to required servers. (3) Restrict arbitrary user SSH access to and from jump box servers."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="ms-rpc" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;ms-rpc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:35:45Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;MS-RPC and SMB&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">MS-RPC and SMB<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-aebdca0afc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:13:10Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Both MS-RPC and SMB don’t immediately allow for lateral movement — other protocols that are built on top of them do (see Figure 4). SMB is used for file transfer and communications, while RPC is used to call remote functions from defined interfaces. RPC is also sometimes carried over SMB, so they’re tightly coupled. They are also notoriously difficult to properly segment, as they are baked into the Windows domain system.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>For example, domain authentication is implemented in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-nrpc/ff8f970f-3e37-40f7-bd4b-af7336e4792f\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Netlogon&lt;/a>, an RPC-based protocol. Domain group policies and logon scripts are stored in a shared folder on the domain controller called &lt;a href=\&#34;https://social.technet.microsoft.com/wiki/contents/articles/8548.active-directory-sysvol-and-netlogon.aspx\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>SYSVOL&lt;/a>, and domain-joined machines access it over SMB.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Blocking off SMB and RPC is practically impossible, without breaking the entire domain. So, what can you do? With SMB, you can create policies based on logic units — most servers and machines shouldn’t talk with one another over SMB, unless the destination is a file server. As such, proper ringfencing segmentation should help mitigate the risk of SMB.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Both MS-RPC and SMB don’t immediately allow for lateral movement — other protocols that are built on top of them do (see Figure 4). SMB is used for file transfer and communications, while RPC is used to call remote functions from defined interfaces. RPC is also sometimes carried over SMB, so they’re tightly coupled. They are also notoriously difficult to properly segment, as they are baked into the Windows domain system. </p>
<p>For example, domain authentication is implemented in <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-nrpc/ff8f970f-3e37-40f7-bd4b-af7336e4792f" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Netlogon</a>, an RPC-based protocol. Domain group policies and logon scripts are stored in a shared folder on the domain controller called <a href="https://social.technet.microsoft.com/wiki/contents/articles/8548.active-directory-sysvol-and-netlogon.aspx" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">SYSVOL</a>, and domain-joined machines access it over SMB.</p>
<p>Blocking off SMB and RPC is practically impossible, without breaking the entire domain. So, what can you do? With SMB, you can create policies based on logic units — most servers and machines shouldn’t talk with one another over SMB, unless the destination is a file server. As such, proper ringfencing segmentation should help mitigate the risk of SMB.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for SMB. (1) Restrict cross-segment SMB. (2) Allow SMB to domain controllers, but increase the alert sensitivity on them in your other security tools." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-c42b83a07b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:17:34Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;94182de3-b76c-4af4-8d5a-927e0f4a299a&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:17:22Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-five.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-five.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for SMB. (1) Restrict cross-segment SMB. (2) Allow SMB to domain controllers, but increase the alert sensitivity on them in your other security tools."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-495df74519&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:14:16Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>A similar approach can be applied to RPC, but it can be even more restrictive, since we don’t need to allow RPC traffic to file servers, unlike in SMB. Also, since RPC is handled in user mode, it is possible to create segmentation policies based on the target service or process, so you only need to deal with RPC interfaces that can be abused for lateral movement (and only if you have a segmentation agent that can handle process- or service-based rules).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The following table shows RPC interfaces that should be managed to prevent lateral movement.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>A similar approach can be applied to RPC, but it can be even more restrictive, since we don’t need to allow RPC traffic to file servers, unlike in SMB. Also, since RPC is handled in user mode, it is possible to create segmentation policies based on the target service or process, so you only need to deal with RPC interfaces that can be abused for lateral movement (and only if you have a segmentation agent that can handle process- or service-based rules). </p>
<p>The following table shows RPC interfaces that should be managed to prevent lateral movement.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-2cf650ee73&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:57:25Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;table>\r\n&lt;tbody>&lt;tr>&lt;th>&lt;p>Technique&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;th>&lt;p>Usage&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;th>&lt;p>RPC interface&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;th>&lt;p>Destination process&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;th>&lt;p>Service&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/th>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1569/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>PsExec&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp; &amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>Communicating with the service manager to execute remote binaries. Usually used after copying malicious binary remotely with SMB&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-scmr/705b624a-13de-43cc-b8a2-99573da3635f\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>MS-SCMR&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>services. exe&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1112/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>Registry&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>Modifying the registry remotely to achieve persistence, run logon scripts or weaken security&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-rrp/0fa3191d-bb79-490a-81bd-54c2601b7a78\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>MS-RRP&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td rowspan=\&#34;3\&#34;>&lt;p>svchost.exe&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>RemoteRegistry&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1053/005/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>Task Scheduler&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>Creating scheduled tasks remotely for command execution&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-tsch/d1058a28-7e02-4948-8b8d-4a347fa64931\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>MS-TSCH&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>Schedule&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;/tr>&lt;tr>&lt;td>&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/003/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>&lt;u>DCOM&lt;/u>&lt;/a>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/td>\r\n&lt;td>&lt;p>Another abstraction layer above RPC. <div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-b4662bc7b1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:17:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Fig. 4: RPC interfaces that can be used for lateral movement&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Fig. 4: RPC interfaces that can be used for lateral movement</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-92fd549223&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:17:24Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Since not all operations over those RPC interfaces are malicious (for example, some monitoring solutions and watchdogs interact with the service manager remotely to check for service health), we recommend surveying existing RPC communications. If they aren’t normally accessed remotely (or if you can narrow down the source list), we recommend you create segmentation policies around them for the extra security benefit.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Since not all operations over those RPC interfaces are malicious (for example, some monitoring solutions and watchdogs interact with the service manager remotely to check for service health), we recommend surveying existing RPC communications. If they aren’t normally accessed remotely (or if you can narrow down the source list), we recommend you create segmentation policies around them for the extra security benefit.</p>

</div>

  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for MS-RPC. (1) Restrict communications to processes or services that host RPC interfaces that can be used for lateral movement. (2) Allow traffic that originates from servers that are used for monitoring or watchdogs." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-0ce69c107a&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:18:17Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;1d589cc3-50fe-48b2-9123-c5b7179374a6&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:18:04Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-six.jpg&#34;}}}">
