<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="winrm" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;winrm&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:36:16Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;PowerShell, WMI, WinRM&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">PowerShell, WMI, WinRM</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-60ad1c4d76&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:30:32Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Both PowerShell and WMI are capable of interacting with remote machines, and that interaction is “powered” by &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/winrm/about-windows-remote-management\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Windows Remote Management&lt;/a> (WinRM). Since the legitimate usage is usually remote management or monitoring (with WMI), there should be few use cases in your network. It should be possible to create segmentation policies that restrict arbitrary usage and allow it only from monitoring servers or IT machines.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Of course, outliers are possible and we’ve seen a few cases where remote PowerShell was used extensively by developers for convenience; it would probably require a case-by-case decision.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Both PowerShell and WMI are capable of interacting with remote machines, and that interaction is “powered” by <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/winrm/about-windows-remote-management" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Windows Remote Management</a> (WinRM). Since the legitimate usage is usually remote management or monitoring (with WMI), there should be few use cases in your network. It should be possible to create segmentation policies that restrict arbitrary usage and allow it only from monitoring servers or IT machines. </p>
<p>Of course, outliers are possible and we’ve seen a few cases where remote PowerShell was used extensively by developers for convenience; it would probably require a case-by-case decision.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for Powershell, WinRM and WMI. (1) Restrict arbitrary user usage. (2) Allow IT machines and monitoring servers. (3) Allow specific user usage on a case-by-case basis." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-1c658c61d1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:18:56Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;4c1249bb-8f4e-41bd-b83f-fc914e768893&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:18:45Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-seven.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-seven.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for Powershell, WinRM and WMI. (1) Restrict arbitrary user usage. (2) Allow IT machines and monitoring servers. (3) Allow specific user usage on a case-by-case basis."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="snmp" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;snmp&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:36:26Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;SNMP&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">SNMP<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-dda23f3e0b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:33:03Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Simple Network Management Protocol (SNMP) is a popular monitoring solution, especially for Linux machines. SNMP also has an EXTEND plug-in, that could be abused for remote script execution, as we’ve mentioned in our post about Linux lateral movement (and implemented in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/guardicore/monkey/releases\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Infection Monkey&lt;/a>). Although the EXTEND plug-in is no longer enabled by default for remote commands in newer releases of the SNMP agent, it is still possible to compile an SNMP agent with the plug-in enabled. We’ve also seen machines running an unpatched version that has the EXTEND plug-in enabled.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>Since SNMP is used for monitoring, we recommend allowing SNMP traffic to originate only from monitoring servers, and restricting it from the rest of the network&lt;/b>. We also recommend giving additional attention to EDR alerts originating from the monitoring servers to prevent them from being used as a proxy to the rest of the network by attackers.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When there are multiple monitoring servers used by different products, separation by segmentation of different logical units should also be considered (for example, if you have a monitoring solution for your finance servers, and only for them, don’t allow it to access your web servers).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Simple Network Management Protocol (SNMP) is a popular monitoring solution, especially for Linux machines. SNMP also has an EXTEND plug-in, that could be abused for remote script execution, as we’ve mentioned in our post about Linux lateral movement (and implemented in <a href="https://github.com/guardicore/monkey/releases" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Infection Monkey</a>). Although the EXTEND plug-in is no longer enabled by default for remote commands in newer releases of the SNMP agent, it is still possible to compile an SNMP agent with the plug-in enabled. We’ve also seen machines running an unpatched version that has the EXTEND plug-in enabled.</p>
<p><b>Since SNMP is used for monitoring, we recommend allowing SNMP traffic to originate only from monitoring servers, and restricting it from the rest of the network</b>. We also recommend giving additional attention to EDR alerts originating from the monitoring servers to prevent them from being used as a proxy to the rest of the network by attackers. </p>
<p>When there are multiple monitoring servers used by different products, separation by segmentation of different logical units should also be considered (for example, if you have a monitoring solution for your finance servers, and only for them, don’t allow it to access your web servers).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="r-commands" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;r-commands&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:36:36Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Telnet and the Berkeley r-commands&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Telnet and the Berkeley r-commands<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-bb143392ba&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:37:12Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Telent and the Berkeley r-command are much less common, and have largely been replaced by SSH. We covered them in our Linux lateral movement post. But just because they’re rare does not mean we should ignore their existence. After all, attackers don’t care about commonality, they’ll use whatever means they have available.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>We recommend replacing these protocols with more secure protocols, like SSH, or at the very least encapsulating their traffic in a secure channel&lt;/b>. Where it isn’t possible, the same security practices around SSH apply.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Telent and the Berkeley r-command are much less common, and have largely been replaced by SSH. We covered them in our Linux lateral movement post. But just because they’re rare does not mean we should ignore their existence. After all, attackers don’t care about commonality, they’ll use whatever means they have available. </p>
<p><b>We recommend replacing these protocols with more secure protocols, like SSH, or at the very least encapsulating their traffic in a secure channel</b>. Where it isn’t possible, the same security practices around SSH apply.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="exfiltration" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;exfiltration&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:36:56Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Exfiltration&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Exfiltration<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5641c79e18&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:37:49Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Unless you want to control all outgoing traffic 1984-style, you can’t realistically expect to prevent data exfiltration during attacks using only segmentation. The internet is large and wide, it is not realistic to have an accurate verdict for every site and server that users are connecting to from your network. As such, threat actors can easily camouflage their exfiltration attempts among all the other outbound traffic.&lt;br>\r\n&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Instead of trying to control the outbound traffic, it is more feasible to control who can access sensitive data. The only place where it might be possible to restrict outbound traffic is on servers in the network; unlike user machines, there should be much less variability in their outbound destinations.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Unless you want to control all outgoing traffic 1984-style, you can’t realistically expect to prevent data exfiltration during attacks using only segmentation. The internet is large and wide, it is not realistic to have an accurate verdict for every site and server that users are connecting to from your network. As such, threat actors can easily camouflage their exfiltration attempts among all the other outbound traffic.<br />
</p>
<p>Instead of trying to control the outbound traffic, it is more feasible to control who can access sensitive data. The only place where it might be possible to restrict outbound traffic is on servers in the network; unlike user machines, there should be much less variability in their outbound destinations.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti exfiltration. (1) Restrict outbound traffic destination from servers in the network. (2) Have strict access controls on sensitive files and folders in internal file servers. (3) Ringfence and segment internal databases so they’re accessible on a need-to basis." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-bf5467a0ae&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:19:37Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;df9c5dc0-15cf-4c4d-8f30-e1e996c128bb&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:19:25Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-eight.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-eight.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for anti exfiltration. (1) Restrict outbound traffic destination from servers in the network. (2) Have strict access controls on sensitive files and folders in internal file servers. (3) Ringfence and segment internal databases so they’re accessible on a need-to basis."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="general-segmention" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;general-segmention&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T19:37:29Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;General segmentation workflow&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">General segmentation workflow<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1bfdb2201c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:39:28Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The overarching principle for this entire section is “&lt;b>Just because it exists, does not mean it should be allowed.&lt;/b>” When segmenting a part of the network, whether it’s a business-critical application (like SWIFT), an operational unit (like the domain controller), or an environment (like production servers), the first order of business is to survey the existing traffic (Figure 5).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>After analyzing the existing traffic, you can create policies that allow the relevant flows and restrict the rest (this is also your opportunity to find any misconfigurations that should be handled by the application owner instead of segmentation).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We recommend not implementing a blocking policy immediately, but running in an alerts-only mode for some time. You should move to a restricting policy only after you deem that the policy is running as intended and that the policy violation alerts are at a minimum or controlled amount.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>It is also important to differentiate your current environment (the one that existed before you started segmenting it) and your future environment (the one after you’ve implemented your segmentation policy). When first implementing segmentation, you should use caution and learn the network to avoid breaking things.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Newer additions, however, should be added while considering the existing segmentation policy. Make policy exceptions and allowances where needed for normal operativity, but don’t disregard the existing policy just because you’re expanding the network.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The overarching principle for this entire section is “<b>Just because it exists, does not mean it should be allowed.</b>” When segmenting a part of the network, whether it’s a business-critical application (like SWIFT), an operational unit (like the domain controller), or an environment (like production servers), the first order of business is to survey the existing traffic (Figure 5). </p>
<p>After analyzing the existing traffic, you can create policies that allow the relevant flows and restrict the rest (this is also your opportunity to find any misconfigurations that should be handled by the application owner instead of segmentation). </p>
<p>We recommend not implementing a blocking policy immediately, but running in an alerts-only mode for some time. You should move to a restricting policy only after you deem that the policy is running as intended and that the policy violation alerts are at a minimum or controlled amount. </p>
<p>It is also important to differentiate your current environment (the one that existed before you started segmenting it) and your future environment (the one after you’ve implemented your segmentation policy). When first implementing segmentation, you should use caution and learn the network to avoid breaking things. </p>
<p>Newer additions, however, should be added while considering the existing segmentation policy. Make policy exceptions and allowances where needed for normal operativity, but don’t disregard the existing policy just because you’re expanding the network.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="A flowchart of the general segmentation workflow. It&#39;s a cycle with four parts: analyzing existing traffic, creating the segmentation policy, monitoring policy violations, and moving the policy to blocking mode." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-4842ebb250&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:42:14Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;A flowchart of the general segmentation workflow. It&#39;s a cycle with four parts: analyzing existing traffic, creating the segmentation policy, monitoring policy violations, and moving the policy to blocking mode.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;6ca69b72-3812-4665-953c-b150ebbefc6b&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:42:05Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-workflow.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-workflow.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="A flowchart of the general segmentation workflow. It&#39;s a cycle with four parts: analyzing existing traffic, creating the segmentation policy, monitoring policy violations, and moving the policy to blocking mode."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 5: The general segmentation workflow</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="ringfencing" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;ringfencing&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:22:10Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Ringfencing&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Ringfencing<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-dc7d8164c7&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:43:07Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>With ringfencing, we’re mostly interested in the interfaces of the segment with the rest of the network and with the world. We want to control what comes in and goes out of the part of the network we want to segment without considering what is going on inside the segment.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>With ringfencing, we’re mostly interested in the interfaces of the segment with the rest of the network and with the world. We want to control what comes in and goes out of the part of the network we want to segment without considering what is going on inside the segment.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for ringfencing. (1) Allow communications with network critical servers, like domain controllers or the SIEM. (2) Allow communications with other servers in the network that are necessary for business logic, like a specific database. (3) Limit arbitrary user access to the segment to a need-to basis. (4) Restrict outbound traffic from servers and inbound internet traffic to servers." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-3d28f3b743&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:20:15Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;b1e47003-9b1f-4c9e-9b98-0a1ae510f5ab&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:20:06Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-nine.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-nine.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for ringfencing. (1) Allow communications with network critical servers, like domain controllers or the SIEM. (2) Allow communications with other servers in the network that are necessary for business logic, like a specific database. (3) Limit arbitrary user access to the segment to a need-to basis. (4) Restrict outbound traffic from servers and inbound internet traffic to servers."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="application-ringfencing" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;application-ringfencing&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:22:22Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Application ringfencing&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Application ringfencing<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8407970c9b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T17:45:01Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>We can take ringfencing one step further, and apply policies to individual machines based on their purpose. So,for example, if a server functions only as a database, it should only be given access over the database ports; a web server, over web ports.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Of course, it’s not that simple. There are usually more services that need access to those servers, such as watchdogs, performance monitors, or IT. Usually, those access ports also look very similar to lateral movement techniques, since they usually revolve around some sort of remote control. (For example, remote watchdogs query the service manager, in a similar way to the PsExec lateral movement technique. The only way to distinguish between the calls is deep packet inspection, which is usually not available.)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To overcome this challenge, wherever you need to allow additional traffic besides what should already access the service, we recommend you limit the allowed sources to the segment that should do the monitoring.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition, we can limit user access to sensitive locations that they don’t need. If the database only serves internal applications, there’s little reason to let arbitrary users query it. Blocking arbitrary user access is the most crucial security step in our opinion, since many attacks begin from compromised users.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>We can take ringfencing one step further, and apply policies to individual machines based on their purpose. So,for example, if a server functions only as a database, it should only be given access over the database ports; a web server, over web ports.</p>
<p>Of course, it’s not that simple. There are usually more services that need access to those servers, such as watchdogs, performance monitors, or IT. Usually, those access ports also look very similar to lateral movement techniques, since they usually revolve around some sort of remote control. (For example, remote watchdogs query the service manager, in a similar way to the PsExec lateral movement technique. The only way to distinguish between the calls is deep packet inspection, which is usually not available.)</p>
<p>To overcome this challenge, wherever you need to allow additional traffic besides what should already access the service, we recommend you limit the allowed sources to the segment that should do the monitoring.</p>
<p>In addition, we can limit user access to sensitive locations that they don’t need. If the database only serves internal applications, there’s little reason to let arbitrary users query it. Blocking arbitrary user access is the most crucial security step in our opinion, since many attacks begin from compromised users.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for application ringfencing. (1) Allow communications to servers based on their role, like web traffic to web servers. (2) Allow communications to servers that are required for their operation, like watchdogs, but limit the allowed sources to only the monitoring machines or their segment. (3) Block user access to internal servers that should not be user accessible." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-818fb5388d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:21:00Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;5ecb38e3-9eed-430c-8022-7da1aea100af&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:20:43Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-ten.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-ten.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for application ringfencing. (1) Allow communications to servers based on their role, like web traffic to web servers. (2) Allow communications to servers that are required for their operation, like watchdogs, but limit the allowed sources to only the monitoring machines or their segment. (3) Block user access to internal servers that should not be user accessible."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="microsegmentation" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;microsegmentation&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T21:20:58Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Microsegmentation&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Microsegmentation<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9448e17112&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:14:16Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>With &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/glossary/what-is-microsegmentation.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>microsegmentation&lt;/a>, we’re applying another layer of granularity to our segmentation policy — we separate the machines in the segment based on their role or sensitivity. We can think of it as a hybrid between application ringfencing and general ringfencing. &lt;b>The major difference from ringfencing is that we now also control traffic inside the segment, and don’t automatically trust neighbors&lt;/b>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Our principle here is that we shouldn’t trust traffic from neighboring machines just because we’re inside the same segment. Attackers will use whatever connection they can to propagate throughout the network, regardless of segments.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>So, even if we have the same kind of application server in the segment, there’s no reason for them to be able to communicate with one another on every port and protocol. Microsegmentation means we apply policy rules on all kinds of traffic, even inside the network segment and among machines with the same role.&lt;br>\r\n&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Of course, machines inside the same segment are usually more tightly coupled, so it’s more difficult to add policies without being overly permissive.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>With <a href="/glossary/what-is-microsegmentation" target="_self">microsegmentation</a>, we’re applying another layer of granularity to our segmentation policy — we separate the machines in the segment based on their role or sensitivity. We can think of it as a hybrid between application ringfencing and general ringfencing. <b>The major difference from ringfencing is that we now also control traffic inside the segment, and don’t automatically trust neighbors</b>.</p>
<p>Our principle here is that we shouldn’t trust traffic from neighboring machines just because we’re inside the same segment. Attackers will use whatever connection they can to propagate throughout the network, regardless of segments. </p>
<p>So, even if we have the same kind of application server in the segment, there’s no reason for them to be able to communicate with one another on every port and protocol. Microsegmentation means we apply policy rules on all kinds of traffic, even inside the network segment and among machines with the same role.<br />
</p>
<p>Of course, machines inside the same segment are usually more tightly coupled, so it’s more difficult to add policies without being overly permissive.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="table summarizing the guiding principles for microsegmentation. (1) Restrict arbitrary connections inside the segment. (2) Allow communications inside the segment on a need-to basis." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-f9c395f34f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:21:31Z&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;c88d1a89-730f-4906-a523-e2fbdc8db91b&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-10-04T05:21:22Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/jpeg&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-eleven.jpg&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-from-a-practical-perspective-data-eleven.jpg" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="table summarizing the guiding principles for microsegmentation. (1) Restrict arbitrary connections inside the segment. (2) Allow communications inside the segment on a need-to basis."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-65eec87afb&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T21:06:32Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Depending on how you define the segments in your network, the principles for application ringfencing can often also apply as microsegmentation principles. For example, if we split our network into a user segment, database segment, and web server segment, then the principles defined in &lt;a href=\&#34;#application-ringfencing\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>application ringfencing&lt;/a> are also suitable for microsegmentation. The only addition required is the application of the same principles inside each application segment, among different machines.&lt;br>\r\n&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>However, if our network is split into a finance segment, sales segment, and IT segment, and each segment has a mix of servers and user machines, then we need to be more creative. After applying the general ringfencing strategies to the segments, we must then turn to creating policies among the segments and inside them. We can consider each segment a mini-network; then we can split each one into the different applications and machine types that contrive it. (For example, for a sales segment, we might have a fileserver, database, and user machines.) We can treat each kind of machine as a new segment, and follow the ringfencing or application ringfencing guidelines again.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Figure 6 summarizes the relations among the various segmentation strategies.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Depending on how you define the segments in your network, the principles for application ringfencing can often also apply as microsegmentation principles. For example, if we split our network into a user segment, database segment, and web server segment, then the principles defined in <a href="#application-ringfencing" target="_self">application ringfencing</a> are also suitable for microsegmentation. The only addition required is the application of the same principles inside each application segment, among different machines.<br />
</p>
<p>However, if our network is split into a finance segment, sales segment, and IT segment, and each segment has a mix of servers and user machines, then we need to be more creative. After applying the general ringfencing strategies to the segments, we must then turn to creating policies among the segments and inside them. We can consider each segment a mini-network; then we can split each one into the different applications and machine types that contrive it. (For example, for a sales segment, we might have a fileserver, database, and user machines.) We can treat each kind of machine as a new segment, and follow the ringfencing or application ringfencing guidelines again.</p>
<p>Figure 6 summarizes the relations among the various segmentation strategies.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="A diagram showing a theoretical network. It has an infrastructure segment, a finance segment, and a sales segment. The finance segment has desktop machines and a database server. Segmentation among them is labelled as microsegmentation. The sales segment has desktop machines, a server, and a database. Segmentation among the desktop machines and the servers is labelled as microsegmentation. The infrastructure segment has a domain controller, a monitoring subsegment, and a web servers subsegment. Segmentation between among web servers is microsegmentation. Segmentation among the monitoring subsegment or the domain controller to the finance segment can be considered application ringfencing, while general segmentation among the three segments is general ringfencing." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-984b0ccd37&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:18:15Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;A diagram showing a theoretical network.           <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/segmentation-strategies.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="A diagram showing a theoretical network.     <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 6: Segmentation strategies in an organizational network</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="defense" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;defense&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:24:40Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Other defense layers’ synergies with segmentation&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Other defense layers’ synergies with segmentation<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-e1f696ef9b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:19:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Although proper network segmentation greatly raises the hurdle necessary for threat actors to clear to breach the network, it still shouldn’t be the only defense layer in your arsenal. You need a defense that includes detection, response, and simulation.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Although proper network segmentation greatly raises the hurdle necessary for threat actors to clear to breach the network, it still shouldn’t be the only defense layer in your arsenal. You need a defense that includes detection, response, and simulation.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="detection" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;detection&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:22:40Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Detection&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Detection<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5340ba30b7&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T21:08:31Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>A dedicated and talented enough attacker will probably be able to get anywhere they want, as no system or network is 100% foolproof, and &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/glossary/what-is-zero-day-attack.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>zero-day&lt;/a> vulnerabilities always exist. It’s not necessarily a realistic scenario (since zero-day vulnerability development is costly and can’t be done on a whim), but we believe that it’s better to prepare for the worst than to plant your head in the sand.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>With this approach, we believe that segmentation comes hand-in-hand with detection. Even if the attackers manage to find footholds in the network and move laterally, you have tools in place to detect them and resolve the threat. It could be EDRs for host threat detection, web access monitoring tools, or regular threat hunting activities. The important things are that suspicious activity is detected and alerted, and that you have a team in place to investigate those alerts.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition to detection, there are three added benefits that a segmented network provides over a flat network (Figure 7).&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>It raises the skill level required to breach the network and can deter less-skilled threat actors. Zero-day vulnerabilities aren’t available to most attackers, so given the threat model of your network, a good network segmentation policy might serve as a good enough deterrent against most attackers.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The more hops threat actors have to take in the network, the more chances are that they’ll be detected because of the increased time and steps it takes to complete a full intrusion.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>It might also be possible to direct attackers to “choke points” where they’re more easily identifiable. This can be done through honeypots, canaries, or even just extra vigilance. &lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>A dedicated and talented enough attacker will probably be able to get anywhere they want, as no system or network is 100% foolproof, and <a href="/glossary/what-is-zero-day-attack" target="_self">zero-day</a> vulnerabilities always exist. It’s not necessarily a realistic scenario (since zero-day vulnerability development is costly and can’t be done on a whim), but we believe that it’s better to prepare for the worst than to plant your head in the sand.</p>
<p>With this approach, we believe that segmentation comes hand-in-hand with detection. Even if the attackers manage to find footholds in the network and move laterally, you have tools in place to detect them and resolve the threat. It could be EDRs for host threat detection, web access monitoring tools, or regular threat hunting activities. The important things are that suspicious activity is detected and alerted, and that you have a team in place to investigate those alerts.</p>
<p>In addition to detection, there are three added benefits that a segmented network provides over a flat network (Figure 7).</p>
<ol>
<li><p>It raises the skill level required to breach the network and can deter less-skilled threat actors. Zero-day vulnerabilities aren’t available to most attackers, so given the threat model of your network, a good network segmentation policy might serve as a good enough deterrent against most attackers.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The more hops threat actors have to take in the network, the more chances are that they’ll be detected because of the increased time and steps it takes to complete a full intrusion.</p>
</li>
<li><p>It might also be possible to direct attackers to “choke points” where they’re more easily identifiable. This can be done through honeypots, canaries, or even just extra vigilance. </p>
</li>
</ol>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="An infographic showing the difference between intrusions in a flat network and a segmented network. Both networks consist of a server segment, a domain admin segment, and a domain controller. In the flat network, the attackers can propagate from their infected machine to all parts of the network immediately. In the segmented network, they first move to the network segment, then to the domain admin segment, and finally to the domain controller." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-12808661f9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:27:37Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;An infographic showing the difference between intrusions in a flat network and a segmented network. Both networks consist of a server segment, a domain admin segment, and a domain controller. In the flat network, the attackers can propagate from their infected machine to all parts of the network immediately. In the segmented network, they first move to the network segment, then to the domain admin segment, and finally to the domain controller.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;29e386c7-a860-426b-b7cf-517b197d6881&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:27:26Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/flat-vs-segmented.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/flat-vs-segmented.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="An infographic showing the difference between intrusions in a flat network and a segmented network. Both networks consist of a server segment, a domain admin segment, and a domain controller. In the flat network, the attackers can propagate from their infected machine to all parts of the network immediately. In the segmented network, they first move to the network segment, then to the domain admin segment, and finally to the domain controller."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 7: Flat vs. segmented network intrusion. In the flat network, every part of it is reachable simultaneously and intruders can reach their goal quickly. In a segmented network, attackers have to act procedurally.</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="response" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;response&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:22:49Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Response&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h3 class="cmp-title__text">Response<br />
</h3>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8110ef9c43&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T21:10:02Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Simply detecting threats is not enough, you must also respond quickly to alerts and breaches. According to &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/ransomware-attacks-need-less-than-four-days-to-encrypt-systems/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>reports about ransomware attacks&lt;/a>, breach to encryption only takes a few days. That means you also have only a few days to detect them and drive them out of the network. Granted, as we said earlier, a proper segmentation will slow down the attack, but attacks still need prompt reaction.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Segmentation synergizes with response in two ways.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>&lt;b>It gives you more time to respond&lt;/b> because attacks will now take longer to complete and have more places of friction to generate alerts (where attacker traffic clashes with your segmentation policy).&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>&lt;b>It can be used to respond&lt;/b>. In the same way that you create segmentation policies and rules to restrict and control access to different parts of the network, you can create rules to quarantine assets — so attacks can’t proceed further. Incorporating segmentation in your incident response plans and workflow, and having tools to deploy quarantine rules quickly in case of an emergency, can be pivotal in dealing with network breaches.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Simply detecting threats is not enough, you must also respond quickly to alerts and breaches. According to <a href="https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/ransomware-attacks-need-less-than-four-days-to-encrypt-systems/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">reports about ransomware attacks</a>, breach to encryption only takes a few days. That means you also have only a few days to detect them and drive them out of the network. Granted, as we said earlier, a proper segmentation will slow down the attack, but attacks still need prompt reaction.</p>
<p>Segmentation synergizes with response in two ways.</p>
<ol>
<li><p><b>It gives you more time to respond</b> because attacks will now take longer to complete and have more places of friction to generate alerts (where attacker traffic clashes with your segmentation policy).</p>
</li>
<li><p><b>It can be used to respond</b>. In the same way that you create segmentation policies and rules to restrict and control access to different parts of the network, you can create rules to quarantine assets — so attacks can’t proceed further. Incorporating segmentation in your incident response plans and workflow, and having tools to deploy quarantine rules quickly in case of an emergency, can be pivotal in dealing with network breaches.</p>
</li>
</ol>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingTop-10 title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="simulation" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;simulation&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:23:00Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Simulation&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Simulation<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-57a02d646b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T18:33:47Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>On paper, you may have created the best segmented and secure network possible, and you can detect any attack coming your way. But &lt;a href=\&#34;https://quoteinvestigator.com/2021/05/04/no-plan/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>no plan survives first contact with the enemy&lt;/a>; it is best to have that enemy not be a malicious threat actor.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>That’s where simulation comes in. A &lt;a href=\&#34;https://csrc.nist.gov/glossary/term/red_team\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>red team&lt;/a> can simulate an enemy by trying to hack your systems like a threat actor would, or a network breach automated simulation tool (like Akamai’s open source tool, &lt;a href=\&#34;/content/akamai/en/infectionmonkey.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_self\&#34;>Infection Monkey&lt;/a>) could do that instead.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Simulations can uncover weak spots in your defense that malicious threat actors could exploit. Routinely checking up, and then acting on the results, can greatly increase your network’s security.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>On paper, you may have created the best segmented and secure network possible, and you can detect any attack coming your way. But <a href="https://quoteinvestigator.com/2021/05/04/no-plan/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">no plan survives first contact with the enemy</a>; it is best to have that enemy not be a malicious threat actor. </p>
<p>That’s where simulation comes in. A <a href="https://csrc.nist.gov/glossary/term/red_team" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">red team</a> can simulate an enemy by trying to hack your systems like a threat actor would, or a network breach automated simulation tool (like Akamai’s open source tool, <a href="/infectionmonkey" target="_self">Infection Monkey</a>) could do that instead. </p>
<p>Simulations can uncover weak spots in your defense that malicious threat actors could exploit. Routinely checking up, and then acting on the results, can greatly increase your network’s security.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="title title__paddingBottom-10 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-title" id="summary" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;summary&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/title&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-11T20:23:08Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Summary&lt;br />\r\n&#34;}}">
    
      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Summary<br />
</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8be63db8ed&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-07-12T01:31:27Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Network segmentation is a useful tool to increase network security and deal with network-based threats. It is also a tool that can provide immediate security value, as you don’t have to start with long or arduous segmentation projects, and can instead split your work into multiple subprojects, each one improving the network’s security posture one step at a time.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We’ve provided guidelines to various segmentation policies and strategies to help network admins do just that. We hope that our recommendations are practical and will help keep organizations more secure.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The Akamai Akamai Security Intelligence Group will continue to monitor, study, and publish research on a multitude of security topics. For real-time updates and breaking research, &lt;a href=\&#34;http://www.twitter.com/akamai_research/\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>follow us on Twitter&lt;/a>!&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Network segmentation is a useful tool to increase network security and deal with network-based threats. It is also a tool that can provide immediate security value, as you don’t have to start with long or arduous segmentation projects, and can instead split your work into multiple subprojects, each one improving the network’s security posture one step at a time. </p>
<p>We’ve provided guidelines to various segmentation policies and strategies to help network admins do just that. We hope that our recommendations are practical and will help keep organizations more secure.</p>
<p>The Akamai Akamai Security Intelligence Group will continue to monitor, study, and publish research on a multitude of security topics. For real-time updates and breaking research, <a href="http://www.twitter.com/akamai_research/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">follow us on Twitter</a>!</p>

</div>

    

</div>

      <h2 class="cmp-title__text">Related Blog Posts</h2>
    
</div>

    


</div>

    <h2 class="cmp-teaser__title">
        Call and Register — Relay Attack on WinReg RPC Client
    </h2>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__blog-date">October 19, 2024</div>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__description">Akamai researchers explore a new vulnerability that can be exploited to lead to elevation of privilege attacks against Windows machines.</div>
 
<div class="cmp-teaser__blog-authordetails">by Stiv Kupchik</div>

       <a class="cardlist__action-link" href="/blog/security-research/winreg-relay-vulnerability">Read more<span class="cardlist__action-link_icon"></span></a>

        </div>
    </div>

    <div class="cmp-teaser__cardlist--item  ">
        <div class="cmp-teaser__image cmp-image__wrapper fixed-ratio-16-9 ">

            <a class="cmp-teaser__image-link cmp-image  cmp-image-text-overlay-wrapper" href="/blog/security-research/anonymous-sudan-takedown-akamai-role-ddos">
                <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2024/thumbnails/edge-1080x608-1.png" loading="lazy" alt="This takedown is a huge step toward making the internet a safer place."/>
                
                <div class="cmp-image-text-overlay cmp-image-text-position-middle cmp-image-text-overlay-white-text">
                    <span>This takedown is a huge step toward making the internet a safer place.</span>
                </div>
            </a>
        </div>
        <div class="cmp-teaser__content">
            
    
    
    <h2 class="cmp-teaser__title">
        Anonymous Sudan Takedown: Akamai&#39;s Role
    </h2>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__blog-date">October 16, 2024</div>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__description">The Department of Justice announced the takedown of Anonymous Sudan. Read how Akamai assisted in this effort.</div>
 
<div class="cmp-teaser__blog-authordetails">by Akamai SIRT</div>

       <a class="cardlist__action-link" href="/blog/security-research/anonymous-sudan-takedown-akamai-role-ddos">Read more<span class="cardlist__action-link_icon"></span></a>

    </div>

    <h2 class="cmp-teaser__title">

    </h2>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__blog-date">October 11, 2024</div>
    <div class="cmp-teaser__description">It’s a lot of CVEs, but don’t be scared — leave that for Halloween.  This month, we’ve got 117 total CVEs, and 2 vulnerabilities exploited in the wild.</div>
